<Name>Michael Witt<//Name>< Date>
1491536375921</Date>
<rate>2<//rate>< text>
This is tough......as I think you must consider the horrible weather we had this winter and the effect it had.  But as it stands today in early April, the conditions, specifically in the middle of the fairways and just off the greens, are the worst I've ever seen.   The starter said "you'll lose some balls" and said he'd warned others as well.  But I didn't think he meant in the middle of the fairways!  He was right, I lost at least 3 in the fairways and several other times I had to hunt for several minutes to find them (see pictures for proof).

That being said, I was so impressed with the natural beauty of the area!  The redwoods, view of Mt Tam, and even a deer feeding near the 8th tee.  If this course was well maintained, at least the fairways, I would feel very differently. There were a few holes that made no sense: the direction of #4 is confusing and the yardage is way off, and the tee box on #6 is ridiculous as it's so short you need an 8 or 9 iron, but the overhanging tree is so low you have to punch it to keep it low.

I've included several pictures so you can judge for yourself. In the end I would rather take a jog through this course for exercise than play golf on it, but it's only $21 so I guess you get what you pay for.</text>

<Text>Mill Valley Golf Course has a few pros and many cons which lead me to rate 3 stars.

Pros: -The only golf course in the area
-Friendly staff
-Great price (18 bucks via golf now for 9)
Gorgeous scenery (and im not joking the redwoods on 5 tee were spectacular see photos)

Cons: The incredible difficulty of the course shown through due to the conditions it was in. Including:
-Rock hard greens
-Little to no signage on where the next tee is (i got lost for 15 mins trying to find 6 tee and literally walked into a old abondoned camping ground to find the 7th tee)
-Extreme changes in elevation (this is a bit of a nitpick but having to hoof this nine on foot put me to bed by 8 that night)
-Rough by the greens is longer than Oakmont on a US open year
-I was unable to find yardages for any hole except for par 3 teeboxes making 2nd shots really difficult
-But the creme de la creme of bad is the fairways. Ever wonder how hard it would be to play a course with only rough and no short grass? Come to Mill Valley! I hit 4 out of the 5 of the par 4 fairways today and found myself unable to find my ball twice and the other two times it was half buried leaving no chance to hold those rock hard greens.
-All in all i shot 45 and felt accomplished but not as much fun as i hoped for.

In summary if you come to Mill Valley  do it for the sights because they were top notch. Just dont get your hopes up on breaking par.< /Text><Resp>None</Resp><Date>1493577436268</Date>< pictures>

< text>
I love this place.  I have very fond memories of learning to play on this course and enjoying it the same way everytime I'm there.  It's a fairly easy course, so don't be expecting to see and PGA pros hanging around, and the clubhouse is pretty minimalistic.  But, it has some of the most beautiful scenery surrounding it as it sits in a valley up against a mountain.  Unfortunately as it's a public course, it is subject to city funding and sometimes suffers from poor maintenance.  But, that hardly detracts from the enjoyment.</text>

<rating>4< /rating>< text>
Mill Valley Golf Course is a hidden gem in Marin.  A short 9-hole course (Par 36) that will challenge every aspect of your game weather your a scratch golfer or high HCP.  The course is well maintained and the greens are in great condition. Despite the experience others have had the course has been under new management for over a year. Golf Pro Doug Acton, PGA Professional Trainer (and also hold the course record) teaches lessons at the course.</text>

I've been going to this place for years. When it was ecology, never had a problem. The staff always helpful. Everybody has good days and bad days. Sure everything online is cheaper, but when I need a part I need it now, not two days from now, yes I agree, lkq is a little overpriced and it's only 40% off instead of 50%off sale days, but the inventory control is outstanding. I used to spend sometimes all day looking for parts when it was ecology. If you aren't familiar with their inventory system I'll give you a brief description.  You don't need an account you can use this system anyway, but I suggest you create on its totally free. They keep a eye out for you about cars your interested in when one comes on the yard they notify you by email. But that's not even the best part. This is; go on line to a. lqk location near you. Type in the vehicle you have and they will tell you which  section, the row# and the space# it's in, also the date they got it, even it's color. If they don't have it at that yard lookup the next yard. They also have a parts interchange, that is now user friendly, again type in your vehicle and the part you need and they'll tell you what other car uses the same part. It saves so much time. So what. the price is a little higher. It's worth it.
LKQ AWESOME< /Text>

I am an MBA student myself. < text>
I began classes looking for a second degree, first degree from a large top tier research institution. Its a neat concept but they don't execute their own concept. I did not attempt to complete any assignments, but peer discussion boards are not a way to conduct learning, it should only be used as an additional tool for those who desire it and not a part of a graded assignment. The large majority of graded first semester class assignments were asking students to make peer discussion board posts about a vague question or premise and respond to one another. After reading my peers posts and their response to "instructor" feedback, concise and accurate post will not score you points, long incoherent run-on paragraphs appear to be what they want people to waste time doing. I wouldn't recommend this organization to anyone unless maybe if there were literally no other options on Earth. If you are looking to learn by watching lectures or reading information, then studying and practicing, and then being tested... you will be sorely disappointed. They think that peer chat boards can 100% replace teaching... their "instructors" are simply chat board moderators who do not contribute to the teaching/leaning at all, they just critique people's posts. After seeing how this organization was attempting to operate I withdrew and then for the next 6 months continued to receive marketing emails from an "academic advisor" who had a poor grasp of the English language. Props for being multilingual, but in this case you are simply pushing people away with the annoyance. Before I dive into what I think here, I would really like to express the fact that I'm kinda fed up with other reviews saying stuff like " the material is no better than Wikipedia" or things of a similar nature. And also, I feel bad for people who may have problems with their advisor(s) according to the reviews as well.

Anyways, I see a lot more positives than negatives in this University, such as great teachers (or more like facilitators) that know how to lead the classes well and give me assignments in an appropriate fashion most of the time and also that they are quite challenging for a 5-term - 9 weeks each term - University.

However, my biggest problem is with the student grading system, which really needs to change because I would agree that students shouldn't be handed so much responsibility to be grading each other and the teacher just checks the grades for fairness? Well, the University of Minnesota does this concept way better and I think the UOPeople should take notes from the University of Minnesota because the teachers should be REALLY doing the grading, and the students should just "grade" each other as a personal exercise, nothing more.  I do hope the student grading system changes big time because EVERYONE, not just junior and senior students, could really benefit from the way the UOM does it, at least in the way I proposed it.

This school,  in spite of the negatives, though, is a great makeshift option, at least for anyone who has financial problems or people who want to study in a quarter instead of a semester system. It's not my dream or ideal school, but considering UOPeople's situation, they are doing really well at meeting their purposes.  I do hope the UOPeople takes what I say into consideration, however, thinking through my initial review of this place and ALL of the school's policies in place, the policies themselves are all pretty decently backed for all the flaws and degree of peculiarity they have, but they could still be better, especially that darn student grading system. That is all.</text>

Daniel Stan<//name>
<date>1596461186305<//date><rate>1<//rate>< text>
If you already hold a Bachelor's or Master's degree from a US school and you are looking for a second bachelor's degree, this school is not for you. If it's computer science, you are better off elsewhere. This school is for people who have no other means to get an education and rightfully so.
I hold a bachelor's and a master's degree in statistics and I was hoping to do their CS bachelors for fun and because it was cheaper but it's been a tug of war with their transfer policy.

I first enrolled with them when they did not accept transfer credits and I dropped out because they wanted to make me retake all the General Ed classes that I had already done from a regionally accredited school. Indeed that was a waste of time as I believed my time should be spent learning computer science courses like programming.

In the last couple of years, they've started accepting transfer credit and I reapplied again only to be given a lot of headaches. They make you take 5 foundational classes before you begin the CS program. I expected the foundational classes to be computer science classes but no. About 4 out of the 5 classes were general education classes which I intended to transfer.

I do not want to discuss my class experience in 2014, which was horrible BTW. It seems they still kept their peer evaluation which sucked.
Overall if you are in the US and you are looking for a second degree in CS, UoPeople is not the best route to go. I had to search google to find other regionally accredited online colleges where I could do my CS degree with about 75% credit transfer. Fort Hays gave me that.

UoPeople surely plays a role in educating people in/from poor and developing countries or countries where access to education is non-existent. It also plays a role in helping lower-class Americans, refugees, and asylum seekers get an affordable education. However, that is just as far as it goes. If you do not belong to any of these groups or you are a second-degree seeker with a RA degree, you are better off attending an online community college/college for CS. Their advisers were superb in replying to emails and that's the only positive. Donating that application fee to a COVID response NGO  or to the homeless would have been a better use of the $60 application fee.< /text>

<Date>1603981176869</Date><Resp>{'time': 1604329592888, 'text': "Hi David,\n\nWe have received your comments regarding the peer-to-peer learning, you are not the first one to raise the issue.\n\nWe understand your perspective, as there is a steep learning curve in the first year when it comes to adjusting to peer assessment. That said, please rest assured that if you keep up and continue your progress you will realize the advantage of our pedagogy.\n\nIn addition, according to our research, peer assessment is the grading method that our advanced students, starting from the second year, appreciate the most. Being responsible not only for one's own learning but also for that of one's classmates increases commitment to study and enhances the experience. There is a lot to be gained from peer review, both from receiving and giving feedback. It encourages students to be more critical of their own work and perfect their skills while it offers the opportunity to assist others.\n\nPeer assessment allows a diversity of opinions to be brought to the table, which is a great learning experience as our student body comprises individuals from myriad cultures and backgrounds. Furthermore, peer assessment helps prepare students for the workplace, where assessment by colleagues and constructive criticism are key components of professional development. Peer assessment is also well-regarded in academia and there is much evidence on its benefits and effectiveness (Magin & Helmore, 2001; Race, Brown & Smith, 2005; Stiggins, 2008).\n\nIf you want to learn more about our grading policies and academic model, feel free to visit our student catalog here, https://www.uopeople.edu/about/uopeople/essential-uopeople-documents/university-catalog/\n\nWe hope this explanation satisfies you. I will be done with my Associate Degree in Health Sciences by next year and University of the People is the best fit for me. The cost is affordable (it is tuition-free but there are exam processing fees to cover the university's costs), the learning is flexible, and most importantly, the curriculum is challenging and of high quality. <UserId.>108688985658306678792< /UserId.><Name>sierra thomas</Name>< date>
1580948296678</date>

< review>
REVIEW OF EDUCATION QUALITY/METHODS AND TOTAL COST OF ATTENDING UNIVERSITY OF THE PEOPLE:
Just to be clear, if you are looking for a stellar education, this is NOT IT!
You get minimal feedback from professors and the people largely responsible for grading your work are peers who know about as much (if not less) about the subject as you do.
Also, all materials are in text/video format, so if you're more of a hands-on learner, you might struggle a bit.

However, if you are looking for an affordable and flexible method of getting your basics out of the way so that you can move on to learning what you REALLY want to learn somewhere else, UoPeople is the place for you!

That being said, the tuition free model is definitely something that is worth perusing and UoPeople seems to be making it work well enough. So voting with your dollar for a good cause is definitely a plus.

Classes have a weekly deadline, but other than that, you can complete your course work on your own time. There are no scheduled skype sessions or timed group chats or scheduled final exams. If you can only complete your work at 3:00am, that's fine. If you can only squeeze in your classes on weekends, that's fine too. You complete the course work on YOUR TIME.

However, there is not a fast track option. Courses are only 8 weeks in length (so taking 2 classes is considered full time, 3 is over-time) so you still earn your degree at the same rate as any other university.

Also, they have gotten access to some really great textbooks (FOR FREE) that other colleges would make you pay $100+ for, so that's another advantage.

Bottom line, If you're a career person looking to further your education to enhance your understanding and performance in your profession, GO SOMEWHERE ELSE.
However, If you're a recent high school graduate who doesn't know what you want to do with your life and don't want to wrack up crippling debt for a degree you may or may not use/single mom who just needs that piece of paper to get a promotion/something along those lines, UNIVERSITY OF THE PEOPLE IS THE PLACE FOR YOU!

*PAYMENT INFORMATION*

P.S. a little information about what they mean by "FREE":
UoPeople is TUITION FREE. This does not mean that the entire education is free - you have a lot of professors, counselors, programmers, admin, etc. who all need to get paid for their time.
To cover this, expect to pay the following fees:
- $60 application fee:
this is very competitive as some universities charge up to $80-$100 application fees. Also, UoPeople doesn't seem to be too picky as to who they accept, so odds are that your application fee will earn you some results.
- $100 testing fee for every final you take:
This is a pay-as-you-go system, so it's not like you have to drop the money for classes you plan to take all at once. This fee is due at the end of the term, so you have about eight weeks to save back $100 per class. That being said, if you have to retake a class YOU WILL HAVE TO PAY THE TESTING FEE A SECOND TIME.
- Transfer fees:
If you are transferring credits you will have to pay a transfer fee. This fee seems to fluctuate based on how many credits you are transferring, but I was able to get 12 credit hours transferred for a $68 fee. Again, this is HIGHLY COMPETITIVE. They transferred every one of my credits that they possibly could, which was very helpful.
Other than that, I have not had to pay for a thing. The tuition is free, the counseling is free, and all of the reading/assignment materials are provided at no cost. Assuming I don't have to re-take a class, I will be able to earn an ASSOCIATES DEGREE FOR LESS THAN $2,600.00 and will not have to go into debt to do so.

THIS IS NOT A CHARITY CASE. THIS IS NOT A SCAM. IT IS A STARTING MODEL FOR TUITION-FREE EDUCATION. JUST KEEP IN MIND THAT THIS IS STILL A NEW MODEL AND THAT YOU GET WHAT YOU PAY FOR.<//review>

This university is great for many reasons, but the peer grading system is a deal breaker. It can never be a fair process if grading is not consistent and done by one professional person.< /Review>
< GmapID>
0x80c2c35dda877d39:0x4a582e1ce0241819< /GmapID>
<Pictures>None<//Pictures>< response>
{'time': 1565162889246, 'text': "Hi Robin, thank you for your review. Yes we know; we are currently looking into the model and plan to improve it. We should mention that according to our research, peer assessment is actually the grading method that our advanced students, starting from the second year, appreciate the most. Being responsible not only for one's own learning but also for that of one's classmates increases commitment to study and enhances the experience. There is a lot to be gained from peer review, both from receiving and giving feedback. It encourages students to be more critical of their own work and perfect their skills at the same time that it offers the opportunity to assist others. Peer assessment allows a diversity of opinions to be brought to the table, which is a great learning experience as our student body comprises individuals from myriad cultures and backgrounds. Furthermore, peer assessment helps prepare students for the workplace, where assessment by colleagues and constructive criticism are key components of professional development. We agree we can improve this process, and we will. Thank you for your feedback."}<//response>

Because of a fake audience in reviews and promotions I have lost 60$ today .
Which may not be a big amount but like me many people pay 60$ to enter into the university only to know that they cannot afford .

They do provide a scholarship but there is no proof of evidence or promise to be given one.

Below is the detailed information of how much the University charges .

Hi,thanks for getting in touch. Please note that we are a tuition-free online university, as we do not charge our students for their educational instruction, course materials or annual enrollment. However, in order to ensure that our operations remain sustainable; we require that all applicants pay a one-time application processing fee of $60. Undergraduate students are also required to pay $100 per course as course assessment fee; while MBA/M.Ed. students are required to pay $200 per course as course assessment fee.
In order to complete an Associate‚Äôs degree, you will be required to pass 20 courses. Similarly, in order to complete a Bachelor‚Äôs degree, you will be required to pass 40 courses. As the course assessment fee is $100 USD per course, the expected total cost of the Associates program is $2,000 USD, and the Bachelor's program is $4,000 USD. Undergraduate students are not required to pay this full amount in one transaction, but rather, students pay $100 USD course assessment fee when each course is taken.
In order to complete our MBA program, you will be required to pass 12 courses. As the course assessment fee is $200 USD per course, the expected total cost of the MBA program is $2,460 USD. MBA students are not required to pay this full amount in one transaction, but rather, students pay $200 USD course assessment fee when each course is taken.
In order to complete our M.Ed. program, you will be required to pass 13 courses. As the course assessment fee is $200 USD per course, the expected total cost of the M.Ed. program is $2,660 USD. M.Ed. students are not required to pay this full amount in one transaction, but rather, students pay $200 USD course assessment fee when each course is taken.</Review>

< Text>
UoPeople review

UoPeople has helped open the door to a quality education that would otherwise remain closed. The Return on Investment is immense and the skills that you learn when you pursue your degree help you throughout your life. The University is just at its beginning stages, and once more people graduate from the University, more employers will recognize the degree. University of the People is in my opinion, one of the most valuable websites on the web. The most interesting thing about the college, in my opinion, is the fact that the advisory board consists of members of Ivy league colleges in the US, something that brings even more recognition to those who may be skeptical. I am very satisfied with my MBA degree process and when I am finished, I know I will look back and declare that it is one of the best decisions I've ever made in my life. UoPeople employs a Peer to Peer learning philosophy which further helps with learning uniquely. The important thing to realize is that you have an instructor that can modify any erroneous grades, so you are not at the mercy of an angry grader who scores your assignments :).  I am so happy that I found the MBA program at UoPeople and I cannot wait to see the University become more popular and prestigious.<//Text>
